## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the acceleration (dv/dt) of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator as a function of position, velocity, and time. The acceleration is governed by restoring forces (functions of x) and possibly damping forces (functions of v), characteristic of nonlinear oscillator equations of motion.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force proportional to displacement)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (restoring force plus linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring force with damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - x**2) * v (nonlinear velocity-dependent damping)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinear restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Cubic damping oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v**3 + c2 * x**3 (nonlinear damping and restoring)
- Driven nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external forcing)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force approximating pendulum)
- Mixed nonlinear terms: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric nonlinear restoring force)
- Position-velocity coupling: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v + c2 * x**3 (nonlinear coupling between position and velocity)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-dependent nonlinear damping)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-varying stiffness)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope ŌåÆ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects ŌåÆ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay ŌåÆ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior ŌåÆ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects ŌåÆ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) ŌåÆ symmetric potential well with hardening/softening nonlinearity
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to v ŌåÆ linear energy dissipation or gain (damping/antidamping)
- Terms like (1 - x**2)*v ŌåÆ amplitude-dependent damping switching between energy injection and dissipation (limit cycle behavior)
- Even powers of x in restoring force (x**2) ŌåÆ asymmetric potential well breaking spatial symmetry
- Products x*v ŌåÆ phase-space-dependent forces indicating non-conservative coupling
- Odd powers of v (v**3) ŌåÆ nonlinear damping that increases rapidly at high velocities
- Sinusoidal functions of x ŌåÆ bounded restoring force as in pendulum dynamics
- Explicit time-dependent sinusoidal terms ŌåÆ external periodic driving or parametric excitation

I need to determine which candidates can exactly match the ground truth:

**GT: -0.59954989233168*v - 2.79522534599104*x*exp(-Abs(x))**

Let me analyze the structure: this is a linear term in `v` plus `x*exp(-|x|)` scaled by a constant. The function `x*exp(-|x|)` is a specific non-standard basis function.

Key properties of `x*exp(-|x|)`:
- It's an odd function of x
- It behaves like `x` near 0 (since exp(-|x|) Ōēł 1 - |x| + ...)
- It decays to 0 as |x| ŌåÆ Ōł×

Now I need to check if any candidate can exactly reproduce `x*exp(-|x|)` using their basis functions.

**Critical question:** Can any combination of the offered basis functions (polynomials, tanh, sin, log, exp of polynomials, etc.) exactly equal `x*exp(-|x|)`?

Let me analyze key basis function combinations:

1. **Polynomials** (x, x┬│, xŌüĄ, ...): These grow without bound; `x*exp(-|x|)` decays. No finite polynomial works.

2. **tanh(c*x)**: This is odd, bounded, approaches ┬▒1. Not equivalent to `x*exp(-|x|)`.

3. **sin(c*x)**: Periodic, bounded. Not equivalent.

4. **x*log(c*|x|+1)**: This grows like x*log(|x|) for large |x|. Not equivalent (grows, doesn't decay).

5. **x^c (power functions)**: For non-integer c, these have issues with sign for negative x, and don't have the exponential decay.

6. **x*exp(c*x)**: This is NOT `x*exp(-|x|)` because exp(c*x) treats positive and negative x differently, while exp(-|x|) is symmetric in its decay.

7. **x^c * exp(c*x┬▓)**: Setting c negative gives Gaussian-like decay, but `exp(-x┬▓)` ŌēĀ `exp(-|x|)`.

8. **tanh + sin combinations**: These are bounded functions. Their sum with polynomials cannot reproduce the specific decay profile of `x*exp(-|x|)`.

None of the standard basis functions available in the candidates can exactly reproduce `x*exp(-|x|)`. This function has a non-analytic point at x=0 (due to |x|) and exponential decay, which cannot be captured by finite combinations of polynomials, tanh, sin, log, or Gaussian-type exponentials.

Let me verify candidates with `Abs(x)` terms or special structures:

- **Candidate 53**: Has `c2*Abs(x)` - but `|x|` alone can't create `x*exp(-|x|)`.
- **Candidate 28**: Has `c4*log(c5*|x|+1)*|x|^5` - not equivalent.

For candidates with `x*exp(c*x)` (like Candidate 24, 54): `x*exp(c*x)` is NOT `x*exp(-|x|)` since for x<0, exp(cx) with c<0 gives exp(-c|x|) = exp(c*x) which grows, while exp(-|x|) = exp(x) which also... wait. For x<0: exp(-|x|) = exp(x). And exp(c*x) with c=1 gives exp(x). For x>0: exp(-|x|) = exp(-x), and exp(c*x) with c=-1 gives exp(-x). So we'd need c=1 for x<0 and c=-1 for x>0 simultaneously - impossible with a single constant.

After careful analysis, **none** of the candidates can exactly reproduce `x*exp(-|x|)` using their available basis functions.
